2025-02-10T16:16:09.4271480Z             ``seek()`` and ``read()`` methods and must always

2025-02-10T16:16:09.4277970Z             memory-mapped array is kept on disk. However, it can be accessed
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4278990Z             and sliced like any ndarray.  Memory mapping is especially useful
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4279960Z             for accessing small fragments of large files without reading the

2025-02-10T16:16:09.4281330Z         allow_pickle : bool, optional

2025-02-10T16:16:09.4283180Z             disallowing pickles include security, as loading pickled data can
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4284230Z             execute arbitrary code. If pickles are disallowed, loading object
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4285050Z             arrays will fail. Default: False

2025-02-10T16:16:09.4298150Z             data. Default: 'ASCII'
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4313220Z         max_header_size : int, optional
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4314000Z             Maximum allowed size of the header.  Large headers may not be safe
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4315040Z             to load securely and thus require explicitly passing a larger value.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4315890Z             See :py:func:`ast.literal_eval()` for details.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4316830Z             This option is ignored when `allow_pickle` is passed.  In that case
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4317750Z             the file is by definition trusted and the limit is unnecessary.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4318470Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4318910Z         Returns
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4319950Z         -------
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4320600Z         result : array, tuple, dict, etc.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4321930Z             Data stored in the file. For ``.npz`` files, the returned instance
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4323020Z             of NpzFile class must be closed to avoid leaking file descriptors.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4324160Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4324750Z         Raises
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4325710Z         ------
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4350470Z         OSError
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4350790Z             If the input file does not exist or cannot be read.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4351090Z         UnpicklingError
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4351340Z             If ``allow_pickle=True``, but the file cannot be loaded as a pickle.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4351610Z         ValueError
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4351840Z             The file contains an object array, but ``allow_pickle=False`` given.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4352090Z         EOFError
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4352300Z             When calling ``np.load`` multiple times on the same file handle,
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353020Z             if all data has already been read
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353210Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353320Z         See Also
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353440Z         --------
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353590Z         save, savez, savez_compressed, loadtxt
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4353860Z         memmap : Create a memory-map to an array stored in a file on disk.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4354200Z         lib.format.open_memmap : Create or load a memory-mapped ``.npy`` file.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4354490Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4354600Z         Notes
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4354710Z         -----
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4354910Z         - If the file contains pickle data, then whatever object is stored
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4355170Z           in the pickle is returned.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4355410Z         - If the file is a ``.npy`` file, then a single array is returned.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4355700Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, then a dictionary-like object is
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4356030Z           returned, containing ``{filename: array}`` key-value pairs, one for
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4356300Z           each file in the archive.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4356540Z         - If the file is a ``.npz`` file, the returned value supports the
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4356900Z           context manager protocol in a similar fashion to the open function::
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4357520Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4357670Z             with load('foo.npz') as data:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4357860Z                 a = data['a']
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358010Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358200Z           The underlying file descriptor is closed when exiting the 'with'
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358460Z           block.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358580Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358680Z         Examples
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358800Z         --------
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4358940Z         Store data to disk, and load it again:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359120Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359270Z         >>> np.save('/tmp/123', np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]]))
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359500Z         >>> np.load('/tmp/123.npy')
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359680Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359820Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4359960Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360100Z         Store compressed data to disk, and load it again:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360300Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360420Z         >>> a=np.array([[1, 2, 3], [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360610Z         >>> b=np.array([1, 2])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360790Z         >>> np.savez('/tmp/123.npz', a=a, b=b)
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4360980Z         >>> data = np.load('/tmp/123.npz')
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361160Z         >>> data['a']
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361300Z         array([[1, 2, 3],
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361440Z                [4, 5, 6]])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361570Z         >>> data['b']
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361700Z         array([1, 2])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361830Z         >>> data.close()
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4361970Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362140Z         Mem-map the stored array, and then access the second row
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362380Z         directly from disk:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362530Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362670Z         >>> X = np.load('/tmp/123.npy', mmap_mode='r')
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362860Z         >>> X[1, :]
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4362990Z         memmap([4, 5, 6])
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4363120Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4363220Z         """
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4363380Z         if encoding not in ('ASCII', 'latin1', 'bytes'):
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4363640Z             # The 'encoding' value for pickle also affects what encoding
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4363930Z             # the serialized binary data of NumPy arrays is loaded
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4364200Z             # in. Pickle does not pass on the encoding information to
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4364480Z             # NumPy. The unpickling code in numpy.core.multiarray is
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4364770Z             # written to assume that unicode data appearing where binary
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4365190Z             # should be is in 'latin1'. 'bytes' is also safe, as is 'ASCII'.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4365410Z             #
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4365590Z             # Other encoding values can corrupt binary data, and we
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4365880Z             # purposefully disallow them. For the same reason, the errors=
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4366170Z             # argument is not exposed, as values other than 'strict'
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4366440Z             # result can similarly silently corrupt numerical data.
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4366740Z             raise ValueError("encoding must be 'ASCII', 'latin1', or 'bytes'")
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4366980Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4367170Z         pickle_kwargs = dict(encoding=encoding, fix_imports=fix_imports)
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4367400Z     
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4367530Z         with contextlib.ExitStack() as stack:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4367730Z             if hasattr(file, 'read'):
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4367900Z                 fid = file
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4368060Z                 own_fid = False
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4368210Z             else:
2025-02-10T16:16:09.4368390Z >               fid = stack.enter_context(open(os_fspath(file), "rb"))
